[Did you know that core fatigue can affect your soccer headers? 🧠⚽ Latest research shows that when core muscles are fatigued, it not only impacts your power and technique but also changes the way your body compensates during a header. 🚶‍♂️💥 Here’s what happens: Reduced muscle activity in key stabilizers (like the erector spinae and rectus abdominis) leads to less control in the preparation phase. Increased neck muscle activity during the jump phase to help stabilize the head. Reduced jump height and head acceleration, which can affect your header’s power. The takeaway: Fatigue makes headers less efficient and could increase the risk of injury, especially in the neck.
